# big-code-cross-capmarkets-arch-001: Kafka-Flink Streaming Data Flow (Cross-Repo)

## Task

Trace how streaming data flows from Apache Kafka through Apache Flink's connector framework. Map the complete pipeline from Kafka's producer/consumer API, through the Flink connector base framework, to Flink's streaming runtime. Identify the serialization/deserialization boundary between the two systems and explain how Flink's checkpoint mechanism integrates with Kafka's consumer offset commits.

## Context

- **Repositories**: apache/kafka (Java, ~1M LOC) + apache/flink (Java, ~2M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding (cross-repo, capital markets)
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Domain**: Streaming data infrastructure for capital markets (trade ingestion, pricing, risk)

## Architecture Overview

The Kafka-Flink integration spans two independent projects:

1. **Apache Kafka** — Provides the producer/consumer client API, serialization interfaces, and consumer group coordination
2. **Apache Flink** — Provides the Source/Sink API (flink-core), the connector base framework (flink-connector-base), and the SourceOperator runtime integration (flink-runtime)

The Flink Kafka connector (in a separate repo: apache/flink-connector-kafka) extends Flink's connector-base framework and wraps Kafka's consumer/producer APIs. This task focuses on the API contracts in both main repos that the connector bridges.

## Requirements

1. Map Kafka's producer API: Producer interface, KafkaProducer, ProducerRecord, Serializer
2. Map Kafka's consumer API: Consumer interface, KafkaConsumer, ConsumerRecord, Deserializer, OffsetAndMetadata
3. Map Flink's Source API: Source, SourceReader, SplitEnumerator interfaces
4. Map Flink's connector-base framework: SourceReaderBase, SplitReader, RecordEmitter
5. Map Flink's serde boundary: DeserializationSchema, SerializationSchema
6. Trace the checkpoint-offset integration: SourceOperator.snapshotState() -> SourceReader -> KafkaConsumer.commitSync()

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- kafka/clients/src/.../Producer.java — role in data flow
- flink/flink-core/src/.../Source.java — role in data flow
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Kafka producer: ProducerRecord -> Serializer -> KafkaProducer
2. Kafka consumer: KafkaConsumer -> Deserializer -> ConsumerRecord -> OffsetAndMetadata
3. Flink Source API: Source -> SourceReader -> SplitEnumerator
4. Flink connector-base: SourceReaderBase -> SplitReader -> RecordEmitter
5. Flink serde: DeserializationSchema / SerializationSchema
6. Flink runtime: SourceOperator (checkpoint -> offset commit)
...

## Analysis
[Detailed cross-repo architectural analysis including:
- How Kafka's consumer API is wrapped by Flink's SplitReader
- The dual serialization boundary (Kafka Serializer/Deserializer + Flink Schema)
- How checkpoint completion triggers Kafka offset commits
- The consumer group coordination model
- Thread architecture: Kafka's Fetcher/Sender vs Flink's SplitFetcherManager]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary of the Kafka-Flink data flow]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find files from BOTH repos (Kafka client API + Flink Source/connector-base)?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct cross-repo data flow?
- Architectural coherence: Did you identify the serialization boundary and checkpoint-offset integration?

## Kafka Producer API
- `Producer<K,V>` interface → `KafkaProducer<K,V>` implementation
- `send(ProducerRecord<K,V>)` → serializes key/value via `Serializer<T>.serialize(topic, headers, data) → byte[]`
- Serialized bytes → `RecordAccumulator.append()` → batched into `ProducerBatch`/`MemoryRecords`
- `Sender` (background `SenderThread`) → drains accumulator → `NetworkClient` → `ProduceRequest` to broker
- Acks/callbacks come back via `handleProduceResponse`

## Kafka Consumer API
- `Consumer<K,V>` interface → `KafkaConsumer<K,V>` delegates to `ConsumerDelegate`
- `subscribe(topics)` / `assign(partitions)` for topic selection
- `poll(Duration)` → internally calls `Fetcher.sendFetches()` → `FetchRequest` to brokers → `FetchResponse`
- `AbstractFetch.handleFetchResponse()` → creates `CompletedFetch` objects buffered in `FetchBuffer`
- `CompletedFetch.fetchRecords()` → `parseRecord()` → `Deserializer.deserialize(topic, headers, bytes) → T` → `ConsumerRecord<K,V>`
- `ConsumerRecord` carries: topic, partition, offset, timestamp, key, value, headers
- `commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)` / `commitAsync()` for offset commits

## Flink Source API (FLIP-27)
- `Source<T, SplitT, EnumChkT>` interface extends `SourceReaderFactory`
  - `getBoundedness()` → CONTINUOUS_UNBOUNDED for Kafka
  - `createEnumerator(SplitEnumeratorContext)` → new SplitEnumerator
  - `restoreEnumerator(SplitEnumeratorContext, EnumChkT)` → restored from checkpoint
  - `getSplitSerializer()` → `SimpleVersionedSerializer<SplitT>`
  - `getEnumeratorCheckpointSerializer()` → `SimpleVersionedSerializer<EnumChkT>`

## What the Document Covers

### 1. Kafka Producer API
Traces `Producer<K,V>` → `KafkaProducer` → `doSend()`, where `Serializer<T>.serialize(topic, headers, data) → byte[]` converts typed keys/values to bytes. The bytes are batched in `RecordAccumulator` (`ProducerBatch` / `MemoryRecords`) and drained by the background `Sender` thread via `NetworkClient` as `ProduceRequest`s.

### 2. Kafka Consumer API
Traces `KafkaConsumer.poll()` → `Fetcher.sendFetches()` → `FetchResponse` → `CompletedFetch` buffered in a `FetchBuffer` → `CompletedFetch.parseRecord()` which calls `Deserializer.deserialize(topic, headers, ByteBuffer)` to produce a fully typed `ConsumerRecord<K,V>` carrying topic, partition, offset, timestamp, key, value, and headers.

### 3. Flink Source / SplitEnumerator API (FLIP-27)
Documents `Source<T,SplitT,EnumChkT>` as a factory with `createEnumerator` / `restoreEnumerator`, and the lifecycle of both `SplitEnumerator` (runs in JobManager; `handleSplitRequest`, `addSplitsBack`, `snapshotState`) and `SourceReader` (runs in TaskManager; `pollNext`, `snapshotState`, `notifyCheckpointComplete`).

In that case, the\n    41       * implementation may either decide to return without throwing an exception, or it can just\n    42       * throw an interrupted exception. You can use this setting to bound the time to finish a rebalance, but\n155: *     you risk slower progress if the consumer cannot actually call {@link #poll(Duration) poll} often enough.</li>\n156: *     <li><code>max.poll.records</code>: Use this setting to limit the total records returned from a single\n157: *     call to poll. This can make it easier to predict the maximum that must be handled within each poll\n158: *     interval. By tuning this value, you may be able to reduce the poll interval, which will reduce the\n164: * the consumer to continue calling {@link #poll(Duration) poll} while the processor is still working.\n169: * from poll until after thread has finished handling those previously returned.\n189: *         ConsumerRecords&lt;String, String&gt; records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n228: *         ConsumerRecords&lt;String, String&gt; records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n234: *             consumer.commitSync();\n242: * would be considered consumed after they were returned to the user in {@link #poll(Duration) poll}. It would then be\n255: * you must consume all data returned from each call to {@link #poll(Duration)} before any subsequent calls, or before\n260: * The above example uses {@link #commitSync() commitSync} to mark all received records as committed. In some cases\n267: *             ConsumerRecords&lt;String, String&gt; records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(Long.MAX_VALUE));\n273: *                 consumer.commitSync(Collections.singletonMap(partition, records.nextOffsets().get(partition)));\n282: * Thus, when calling {@link #commitSync(Map) commitSync(offsets)} you should use {@code nextRecordToBeProcessed.offset()}\n312: * Once assigned, you can call {@link #poll(Duration) poll} in a loop, just as in the preceding examples to consume\n404: * on the specified paused partitions respectively in the future {@link #poll(Duration)} calls."

So the offset saved in the checkpoint = the offset of the last processed record + 1 (next to fetch)\n\n3. The analysis is grounded in the actual source code of both repositories.\n\nThe six layers examined, in order of data flow, are:\n\n1. **Kafka Producer API** \u2013 how application records become network bytes  \n2. **Kafka Consumer API** \u2013 how network bytes become `ConsumerRecord` objects  \n3. **Flink Source / SplitEnumerator API** \u2013 the FLIP-27 split-coordination model  \n4. **Connector-Base Framework** \u2013 `SourceReaderBase`, `SplitFetcher`, `SplitReader`, `RecordEmitter`  \n5. **Serde Boundary** \u2013 `DeserializationSchema` / `SerializationSchema` vs. Kafka's own serde  \n6. **Checkpoint-Offset Integration** \u2013 `SourceOperator.snapshotState()` and exactly-once guarantees  \n\n---\n\n## 1. Kafka Producer API\n\n### Public Interface\n\n```\norg.apache.kafka.clients.producer.Producer<K, V>   (interface)\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 KafkaProducer<K, V>                          (implementation)\n```\n\n**Key method:**\n```java\nFuture<RecordMetadata> send(ProducerRecord<K, V> record, Callback callback)\n```\n\n`ProducerRecord` is the wire-neutral envelope:\n\n| Field | Type   \u2514\u2500 handleProduceResponse(ClientResponse)  [callback path]\n```\n\nThe call-back invokes registered `Callback` instances per batch, completing the `Future<RecordMetadata>` returned to the Kafka Consumer API\n\n### Public Interface\n\n```\norg.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.Consumer<K, V>   (interface)\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 KafkaConsumer<K, V>                          (thin fa\u00e7ade)\n       \u2514\u2500\u2500 ConsumerDelegate<K, V>                  (actual implementation via ConsumerDelegateCreator)\n```\n\n**Key methods:**\n```java\nvoid subscribe(Collection<String> topics)        // group-managed partition assignment\nvoid assign(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) // manual assignment\nConsumerRecords<K, V> poll(Duration timeout)\nvoid commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets)\nvoid commitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, OffsetCommitCallback cb)\n```\n\n### Fetch and Deserialization Path\n\n`poll()` drives the entire I/O cycle. Internally:\n\n```\nConsumerDelegate.poll(timeout)\n  \u2514\u2500 Fetcher.sendFetches()\n       \u2514\u2500 NetworkClient.send(FetchRequest to broker)\n  \u2514\u2500 AbstractFetch.handleFetchResponse(ClientResponse)\n       \u2514\u2500 FetchResponse response = (FetchResponse) resp.responseBody()\n            for each TopicPartition in responseData:\n                CompletedFetch completedFetch = new CompletedFetch(...)\n                fetchBuffer.add(completedFetch)\n  \u2514\u2500 CompletedFetch.fetchRecords(fetchConfig, deserializers, maxRecords)\n       \u2514\u2500 parseRecord(deserializers, partition, leaderEpoch, ...)\n```\n\nThe decisive deserialization step inside `CompletedFetch.parseRecord()`:\n\n```java\n// CompletedFetch.java lines 312\u2013332\nByteBuffer keyBytes   = record.key();\nByteBuffer valueBytes = record.value();\n\nK key   = keyDeserializer.deserialize(partition.topic(), headers, keyBytes);\nV value = valueDeserializer.deserialize(partition.topic(), headers, valueBytes);\n\nreturn new ConsumerRecord<>(\n    partition.topic(), partition.partition(), record.offset(),\n    record.timestamp(), timestampType,\n    keyBytes  == null ? Flink Source / SplitEnumerator API (FLIP-27)\n\nThe FLIP-27 source model decouples *split discovery* (runs in the JobManager) from *split reading* (runs in each TaskManager).\n\n### Source Interface\n\n```\norg.apache.flink.api.connector.source.Source<T, SplitT extends SourceSplit, EnumChkT>\n  extends SourceReaderFactory<T, SplitT>\n```\n\n**Methods:**\n\n| Method | Description |\n|--------|-------------|\n| `Boundedness getBoundedness()` | `BOUNDED` or `CONTINUOUS_UNBOUNDED` (Kafka = unbounded) |\n| `SplitEnumerator<SplitT,EnumChkT> createEnumerator(SplitEnumeratorContext<SplitT>)` | Fresh start: create enumerator and begin topic/partition discovery |\n| `SplitEnumerator<SplitT,EnumChkT> restoreEnumerator(SplitEnumeratorContext<SplitT>, EnumChkT)` | Restore from checkpoint state |\n| `SimpleVersionedSerializer<SplitT> getSplitSerializer()` | Serializes splits sent across the network (enumerator \u2192 reader) and stored in checkpoints |\n| `SimpleVersionedSerializer<EnumChkT> getEnumeratorCheckpointSerializer()` | Serializes the enumerator's own checkpoint |\n\nThe `Source` acts as a factory. The actual parallelism comes from the two sub-components it creates.\n\n### SplitEnumerator\n\n```\norg.apache.flink.api.connector.source.SplitEnumerator<SplitT extends SourceSplit, CheckpointT>\n  implements AutoCloseable, CheckpointListener\n```\n\nRuns as part of the **SourceCoordinator** on the JobManager (single instance, not parallelized).\n\n**Lifecycle:**\n\n| Method | When Called | Contract |\n|--------|-------------|----------|\n| `start()` | After construction | Begin scanning Kafka topics for partitions; schedule periodic re-discovery for new partitions |\n| `addReader(int subtaskId)` | TaskManager registers | Typically triggers initial split assignment |\n| `handleSplitRequest(int subtaskId, String hostname)` | Reader sends `RequestSplitEvent` | Assign the next available split; use hostname for rack-awareness if desired |\n| `addSplitsBack(List<SplitT>, int subtaskId)` | TaskManager fails post-checkpoint | Return unprocessed splits to the pending pool for reassignment |\n| `handleSourceEvent(int subtaskId, SourceEvent)` | Custom reader \u2192 enumerator messages | Optional protocol extension |\n| `CheckpointT snapshotState(long checkpointId)` | Checkpoint trigger | Return the set of unassigned splits (already-assigned splits are stored in the reader state, not here) |\n| `notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId)` | Checkpoint finalized | Optional: notify external system |\n| `close()` | Job teardown | Release resources |\n\nAssignment is made via `SplitEnumeratorContext`:\n```java\ncontext.assignSplit(SplitT split, int subtaskId);\ncontext.signalNoMoreSplits(int subtaskId);\n```\n\n### SourceReader\n\n```\norg.apache.flink.api.connector.source.SourceReader<T, SplitT extends SourceSplit>\n  implements AutoCloseable, CheckpointListener\n```\n\nRuns inside each **TaskManager** task. One instance per parallel subtask.\n\n**Lifecycle:**\n\n| Method | When Called | Contract |\n|--------|-------------|----------|\n| `start()` | After creation in `open()` | Send `ReaderRegistrationEvent` to coordinator; initialize internal fetchers |\n| `InputStatus pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output)` | Task mailbox loop | **Must be non-blocking.** Dequeue one record, emit to `output`, return `MORE_AVAILABLE` / `NOTHING_AVAILABLE` / `END_OF_INPUT` |\n| `CompletableFuture<Void> isAvailable()` | Runtime, after `NOTHING_AVAILABLE` | Return a future that completes when data may be available; drives non-blocking I/O |\n| `void addSplits(List<SplitT>)` | Enumerator assigns splits | Hand splits to internal fetchers for consumption |\n| `void notifyNoMoreSplits()` | Enumerator exhausted | Transition toward end-of-input once current splits finish |\n| `List<SplitT> snapshotState(long checkpointId)` | Checkpoint barrier arrives | Return serializable snapshot of each split's current read position |\n| `notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId)` | Checkpoint acknowledged | Used by Kafka connector to commit offsets to Kafka's own offset store |\n| `pauseOrResumeSplits(Collection<String>, Collection<String>)` | Watermark alignment | Suspend/resume individual partition readers |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Connector-Base Framework\n\nThe `flink-connector-base` module provides a production-quality skeleton that implements `SourceReader` using a fetcher-thread / mailbox-thread handover protocol.\n\n### Class Hierarchy\n\n```\nSourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT, SplitStateT>   implements SourceReader<T, SplitT>\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT>           manages fetcher wraps KafkaConsumer)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>   thread-safe handover channel\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>         converts E \u2192 T, advances split state\n```\n\nType parameters:\n\n| Parameter | Meaning | Kafka Example |\n|-----------|---------|---------------|\n| `E` | Raw element from `SplitStateT` | Mutable per-split state | `KafkaPartitionSplitState` (holds current offset) |\n\n### SourceReaderBase\n\nThe main recordEmitter;\nSplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT> splitFetcherManager;\n```\n\n**`pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output)`** \u2013 core dispatch loop (mailbox thread):\n\n```\n1. getNextFetch(output)\n   \u2514\u2500 elementsQueue.poll()              // non-blocking dequeue\n        \u2514\u2500 RecordsWithSplitIds<E>       // batch from a fetcher thread\n2. recordsWithSplitId.nextSplit()       // advance to next split in the batch\n3. recordsWithSplitId.nextRecordFromSplit()  // pull one raw E record\n4. recordEmitter.emitRecord(record, currentSplitOutput, currentSplitContext.state)\n   \u2514\u2500 DeserializationSchema.deserialize(record.value()) \u2192 T\n   \u2514\u2500 splitState.setCurrentOffset(offset + 1)\n   \u2514\u2500 output.collect(deserializedRecord)\n5. return InputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE\n```\n\n**`snapshotState(long checkpointId)`** \u2013 checkpoint path:\n\n```java\n// SourceReaderBase.java line 348\u2013351\nList<SplitT> splits = new ArrayList<>();\nsplitStates.forEach((id, context) ->\n    splits.add(toSplitType(id, context.state)));   // SplitStateT \u2192 SplitT\nreturn splits;\n```\n\nThe abstract method `toSplitType(String splitId, SplitStateT state)` bakes the current mutable offset back into the immutable `SplitT` representation for serialization.\n\n**Abstract methods implementors must provide:**\n\n```java\nSplitStateT initializedState(SplitT split);              // create mutable state from split\nSplitT      toSplitType(String splitId, SplitStateT s);  // mutable state \u2192 immutable split\nvoid        onSplitFinished(Map<String, SplitStateT> finished); // cleanup\n```\n\n### SplitFetcherManager and SplitFetcher\n\n`SplitFetcherManager` owns an `ExecutorService` and a pool of `SplitFetcher` threads. The abstract `addSplits(List<SplitT>)` method decides the threading model:\n\n- `SingleThreadFetcherManager` \u2192 one fetcher for all splits (Kafka connector default); all partitions multiplexed through one `KafkaConsumer`\n- Custom implementations can spawn one thread per split\n\nEach `SplitFetcher` is a `Runnable` with an internal task queue:\n\n```\nSplitFetcher.run()\n  \u2514\u2500 loop: dequeue from taskQueue\n       \u251c\u2500 AddSplitsTask     \u2192 splitReader.handleSplitsChanges(SplitsAddition)\n       \u251c\u2500 RemoveSplitsTask  \u2192 splitReader.handleSplitsChanges(SplitsRemoval)\n       \u251c\u2500 PauseOrResumeSplitsTask\n       \u2514\u2500 FetchTask         \u2192 splitReader.fetch()\n                               \u2514\u2500 put RecordsWithSplitIds<E> onto elementsQueue\n                               \u2514\u2500 elementsQueue.notifyAvailable()  // unblocks the future\n```\n\n### SplitReader\n\n```java\npublic interface SplitReader<E, SplitT extends SourceSplit> extends AutoCloseable {\n    RecordsWithSplitIds<E> fetch() throws IOException;\n    void handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT> splitsChanges);\n    void wakeUp();\n    default void pauseOrResumeSplits(Collection<SplitT> pause, Collection<SplitT> resume);\n}\n```\n\nFor Kafka, the implementation wraps a `KafkaConsumer<byte[], byte[]>`:\n\n- `handleSplitsChanges(SplitsAddition<KafkaPartitionSplit>)` \u2192 calls `kafkaConsumer.assign(newPartitions)` and `kafkaConsumer.seek(partition, offset)` for each new split (using the offset encoded in `SplitT`)\n- `fetch()` \u2192 `kafkaConsumer.poll(pollTimeout)` \u2192 wraps the returned `ConsumerRecords` in a `RecordsWithSplitIds<ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>>`\n- `wakeUp()` \u2192 `kafkaConsumer.wakeup()`\n\n### RecordEmitter\n\n```java\npublic interface RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT> {\n    void emitRecord(E element, SourceOutput<T> output, SplitStateT splitState) throws Exception;\n}\n```\n\nThis is the adapter between the raw Kafka byte world and the Flink record world:\n\n```\nemitRecord(ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]> kafkaRecord,\n           SourceOutput<T> output,\n           KafkaPartitionSplitState splitState):\n\n  T record = deserializationSchema.deserialize(kafkaRecord.value());\n  output.collect(record, kafkaRecord.timestamp());      // emit with event time\n  splitState.setCurrentOffset(kafkaRecord.offset() + 1); // advance position\n```\n\nThe `SourceOutput<T>` wraps both the downstream emission and the watermark pipeline.\n\n### FutureCompletingBlockingQueue \u2013 Thread-Safe Handover\n\n`FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>` is the synchronization point between the `SplitFetcher` threads and the single-threaded task mailbox:\n\n- **Fetcher thread** calls `elementsQueue.put(batch)` \u2192 if queue was empty, calls `notifyAvailable()` which completes the `CompletableFuture<Void>`\n- **Mailbox thread** calls `elementsQueue.poll()` (non-blocking) after the future completes\n- `SourceReader.isAvailable()` returns `elementsQueue.getAvailabilityFuture()`, which the runtime awaits before calling `pollNext()`\n\nThis design ensures `pollNext()` is never blocking and the task thread is never parked waiting for I/O.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Serde Boundary\n\n### DeserializationSchema (Flink)\n\n```\norg.apache.flink.api.common.serialization.DeserializationSchema<T>\n  implements Serializable, ResultTypeQueryable<T>\n```\n\n**Methods:**\n\n```java\nvoid open(InitializationContext context)              // one-time setup, metric registration\nT    deserialize(byte[] message) throws IOException   // single-record, null = skip\nvoid deserialize(byte[] message, Collector<T> out)    // one-to-many (fanout)\nboolean isEndOfStream(T nextElement)                  // EOF sentinel detection\nTypeInformation<T> getProducedType()                  // Flink type system integration\n```\n\nOperates on the **raw value bytes** extracted from `ConsumerRecord.value()`. It is called inside `RecordEmitter.emitRecord()` on the mailbox thread.\n\n### SerializationSchema (Flink)\n\n```\norg.apache.flink.api.common.serialization.SerializationSchema<T>\n  implements Serializable\n```\n\n**Methods:**\n\n```java\nvoid   open(InitializationContext context)\nbyte[] serialize(T element)\n```\n\nUsed by Flink's Kafka sink (`KafkaRecordSerializationSchema`) to convert a Flink record `T` to `byte[]` before constructing a `ProducerRecord<byte[], byte[]>` for `KafkaProducer.send()`.\n\n### Comparison: Flink Serde vs. Kafka Serde\n\n| Dimension | Kafka `Serializer<T>` / `Deserializer<T>` | Flink `SerializationSchema<T>` / `DeserializationSchema<T>` |\n|-----------|------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------|\n| **Scope** | Entire key or value field | Entire value (or key+value via `KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema`) |\n| **Context** | Topic name + headers available | Raw `byte[]` only (unless using `KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema`) |\n| **Invocation site** | Inside `CompletedFetch.parseRecord()` / `KafkaProducer.doSend()` | Inside `RecordEmitter.emitRecord()` |\n| **Thread** | Kafka's I/O loop (poll thread) | Flink's task mailbox thread |\n| **Type info** | None (no Flink type system) | `getProducedType()` integrates with Flink's type system |\n| **One-to-many** | Not supported | `deserialize(byte[], Collector<T>)` supports fanout |\n| **EOF signal** | Not supported | `isEndOfStream(T)` allows bounded source termination |\n| **Initialization** | `configure(Map<String,?>, boolean)` | `open(InitializationContext)` with metric access |\n\n### The Boundary in Practice\n\nWhen the Kafka connector's `SplitReader` calls `kafkaConsumer.poll()`, Kafka's own `Deserializer` is **not used** because the consumer is instantiated with `ByteArrayDeserializer` for both key and value. The resulting `ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>` carries raw bytes. Flink's `DeserializationSchema` is invoked later, in the mailbox thread, inside `RecordEmitter.emitRecord()`. This separation keeps the I/O thread lean and allows Flink-specific features (type information, metrics, one-to-many fanout) at the deserialization stage.\n\n---\n\n## 6. SourceOperator.snapshotState \u2013 Code Walk-Through\n\n```java\n// SourceOperator.java lines 608\u2013612\n@Override\npublic void snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\n splitStates.forEach((id, context) ->\n        splits.add(toSplitType(id, context.state)));\n    return splits;\n}\n```\n\n`splitStates` is a `Map<String, SplitContext<T, SplitStateT>>` keyed by split ID. Each `SplitContext.state` is the `SplitStateT` that was mutated by the `RecordEmitter` on every emitted record:\n\n```java\n// In RecordEmitter.emitRecord():\nsplitState.setCurrentOffset(kafkaRecord.offset() + 1);\n```\n\nSo the checkpoint captures: **for each assigned partition, the offset of the next record to be fetched** (last consumed offset + 1).\n\n### Recovery Path\n\n```\nSourceOperator.initializeState(StateInitializationContext ctx)\n  \u2514\u2500 rawState  = ctx.getOperatorStateStore().getListState(SPLITS_STATE_DESC)\n  \u2514\u2500 readerState = new SimpleVersionedListState<>(rawState, splitSerializer)\n\nSourceOperator.open()\n  \u2514\u2500 List<SplitT> splits = iterableToList(readerState.get())  // restored splits with offsets\n  \u2514\u2500 sourceReader.addSplits(splits)\n       \u2514\u2500 SourceReaderBase.addSplits(splits)\n            \u2514\u2500 splitStates.put(id, new SplitContext(id, initializedState(split)))\n            \u2514\u2500 splitFetcherManager.addSplits(splits)\n                 \u2514\u2500 SplitFetcher task: splitReader.handleSplitsChanges(SplitsAddition)\n                      \u2514\u2500 kafkaConsumer.assign(partitions)\n                      \u2514\u2500 kafkaConsumer.seek(partition, restoredOffset)  // \u2190 key step\n```\n\n`kafkaConsumer.seek(partition, offset)` resets the fetch position to the checkpointed offset. No record between the checkpoint and the failure can be missed; this is the mechanism for **at-least-once** (and with idempotent downstream operators, **exactly-once**) semantics.\n\n### Dual Offset Tracking\n\nFlink maintains **two independent offset stores**:\n\n| Store | Location | Committed By | Used For |\n|-------|----------|-------------|---------|\n| **Flink state backend** | JobManager (distributed store) | `SourceOperator.snapshotState()` on every checkpoint | Recovery after failure; the authoritative source of truth |\n| **Kafka consumer-group store** | Kafka broker (`__consumer_offsets` topic) | `sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete()` \u2192 `kafkaConsumer.commitSync()` | Monitoring, external tooling; **not** used by Flink for recovery |\n\nThis means Flink never relies on Kafka's offset store for recovery\u2014Kafka offsets committed via `notifyCheckpointComplete` are purely informational. A Flink job can always restart from its own checkpoint regardless of what Kafka's offset store says.\n\n### SplitEnumerator Checkpoint\n\nThe `SplitEnumerator` is checkpointed independently by the `SourceCoordinator`:\n\n```\nSourceCoordinator.takeSnapshot(checkpointId)\n  \u2514\u2500 EnumChkT enumState = splitEnumerator.snapshotState(checkpointId)\n  \u2514\u2500 serialized to byte[] via getEnumeratorCheckpointSerializer()\n  \u2514\u2500 stored in coordinator operator state\n```\n\nOn recovery, `Source.restoreEnumerator(enumContext, checkpoint)` rebuilds the enumerator with the set of partitions that had not yet been assigned, preserving the discovery state.\n\n---\n\n## End-to-End Data Flow Summary\n\n```\nApplication Code\n    \u2502\n    \u2502  ProducerRecord<K,V>\n    \u25bc\nKafkaProducer.send()\n    \u2502  Serializer<K>.serialize() \u2192 byte[]\n    \u2502  Serializer<V>.serialize() \u2192 byte[]\n    \u25bc\nRecordAccumulator.append()   \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 Sender thread \u2500\u2500\u2500\u25ba NetworkClient \u2500\u2500\u25ba Kafka Broker\n                                  ProduceRequest\n                                                           \u2502\n                                                    Kafka Partition Log\n                                                     (offset N written)\n                                                           \u2502\n                          FetchRequest \u25c4\u2500\u2500\u2500 NetworkClient \u25c4\u2500\u2500 SplitFetcher thread\n                                \u2502              (Flink TaskManager)\n                                \u2502\n                         AbstractFetch.handleFetchResponse()\n                                \u2502\n                         CompletedFetch buffered in FetchBuffer\n                                \u2502\n                         KafkaConsumer.poll() returns ConsumerRecords<byte[], byte[]>\n                                \u2502\n                         SplitReader.fetch() wraps \u2192 RecordsWithSplitIds<ConsumerRecord<byte[],byte[]>>\n                                \u2502\n                         FutureCompletingBlockingQueue.put(batch)   [fetcher \u2192 mailbox handover]\n                                \u2502\n                         SourceReaderBase.pollNext()                 [mailbox thread]\n                                \u2502  elementsQueue.poll()\n                                \u25bc\n                         RecordEmitter.emitRecord(ConsumerRecord<byte[],byte[]>, output, splitState)\n                                \u2502  DeserializationSchema.deserialize(record.value()) \u2192 T\n                                \u2502  splitState.setCurrentOffset(offset + 1)\n                                \u2502  output.collect(T, timestamp)\n                                \u25bc\n                         Flink downstream operators\n                                \u2502\n                         \u25c4\u2500\u2500 checkpoint barrier \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n                         SourceOperator.snapshotState()\n                                \u2502  sourceReader.snapshotState() \u2192 List<SplitT with offsets>\n                                \u2502  readerState.update(splits)    [Flink state backend]\n                                \u2502\n                         \u25c4\u2500\u2500 notifyCheckpointComplete \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n                         sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete()\n                                \u2502  kafkaConsumer.commitSync(offsetMap)  [Kafka offset store, optional]\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n**1. Byte-array boundary between Kafka and Flink serde layers**  \nThe `SplitReader` always uses `ByteArrayDeserializer`, so Kafka's own deserialization is bypassed. All format logic lives in Flink's `DeserializationSchema`, keeping it on the mailbox thread and avoiding hidden deserialization in the I/O thread.\n\n**2. Mutable `SplitStateT` tracks the live position**  \nRather than storing offsets in a separate map, the connector uses a `SplitStateT` object that is updated in-place by the `RecordEmitter`. At checkpoint time, `toSplitType()` crystallizes that mutable state into the serializable `SplitT`. This avoids any race between offset update and snapshot.\n\n**3. `snapshotState` is synchronous with record emission**  \nBecause `pollNext()` and `snapshotState()` both execute on the task mailbox thread, there is no concurrent mutation of `splitStates` during a snapshot. The offset saved is always consistent with the records that have been emitted to downstream operators.\n\n**4. `notifyCheckpointComplete` for Kafka offset commits is optional**  \nFlink uses its state backend as the single source of truth for recovery. The Kafka consumer-group commit is a convenience for operational tooling (e.g., consumer-lag monitoring). Disabling it does not affect exactly-once processing.\n\n**5. `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue` enables asynchronous source reading**  \nBy returning a `CompletableFuture` instead of blocking, `SourceReader.isAvailable()` lets the Flink runtime schedule other mailbox tasks (timers, watermarks, checkpoint barriers) while waiting for I/O, without parking the task thread.\n",
